# Thread: I can't do Airplane mode at night.. what if my family calls?
**Thread URL:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/i-cant-do-airplane-mode-at-night-what-if-my-family-calls.32461/>
**Subforum:** The EMF Rx
**Posts:** 4
══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
### Rusty — 2026-03-27T12:47:23+0200
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/i-cant-do-airplane-mode-at-night-what-if-my-family-calls.32461/post-369738>

"I can't do Airplane mode at night.. what if my family calls?"

**You can.**

Airplane mode kills Cellular, WiFi & Bluetooth.

IT DOES NOT kill Ethernet.

iPhone → USB Ethernet adapter → Ethernet cable → Router.

Your iPhone gets internet. No wireless. No RF.

Signal rings.
Facetime rings.
WhatsApp rings.
Telegram rings.

Your family can still reach you at 3am.

Fifteen dollars.

That's it!

{ "lightbox\_close": "Close", "lightbox\_next": "Next", "lightbox\_previous": "Previous", "lightbox\_error": "The requested content cannot be loaded. Please try again later.", "lightbox\_start\_slideshow": "Start slideshow", "lightbox\_stop\_slideshow": "Stop slideshow", "lightbox\_full\_screen": "Full screen", "lightbox\_thumbnails": "Thumbnails", "lightbox\_download": "Download", "lightbox\_share": "Share", "lightbox\_zoom": "Zoom", "lightbox\_new\_window": "New window", "lightbox\_toggle\_sidebar": "Toggle sidebar" }

**How to set it up:**

1\. Get a Lightning/USB-C to Ethernet adapter (I'm also using a USB-A to USB-C converter but you can skip that)
2\. Plug an Ethernet cable from your router into the adapter
3\. Plug the adapter into your iPhone
4\. Turn ON Airplane Mode
5\. Make sure WiFi & Bluetooth stay OFF
6\. Turn off the router's WiFi

That's it.

Your body gets 8 hours of peace.

$15 adapter. Wired internet. Full reachability.

No excuses left.

# Thread: Privacy cell carrier
**Thread URL:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/privacy-cell-carrier.32464/>
**Subforum:** The Cave
**Posts:** 1
══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
### DLO — 2026-03-27T19:48:07+0200
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/privacy-cell-carrier.32464/post-369772>

Do some digging [https://www.fastcompany.com/9148100...signed-to-keep-your-phone-from-getting-hacked](https://www.fastcompany.com/91481000/this-new-privacy-focused-phone-service-is-designed-to-keep-your-phone-from-getting-hacked)
You raise a valid concern that deserves serious scrutiny. The Palantir connection is worth digging into.

\## The Palantir Red Flag

Founders John Doyle and Nicholas Espinoza both came from Palantir—a company built on mass surveillance, predictive policing, and government data integration.^1,2^ Palantir's entire business model is:

\- CIA/NSA contracts — In-Q-Tel (CIA's venture arm) was an early investor
\- Defense and intelligence work — helping governments aggregate and analyze surveillance data
\- ICE partnerships — providing infrastructure for immigration enforcement and deportation operations
\- Military targeting — used for drone strike targeting and battlefield intelligence

These aren't "former" employees who left on bad terms. They were senior leadership who helped build surveillance infrastructure.^2^

\---

\## Reasons for Skepticism

\### 1. Surveillance Alumni Building "Privacy" Tools

The same people who spent years helping governments track people are now selling you privacy. The question is whether this is:

\- Genuine redemption/pivot
\- Regulatory arbitrage (profiting from the problem they helped create)
\- Or something worse—controlled opposition or a honeypot

\### 2. Government Backdoor Risk

Palantir's entire existence depends on government contracts and cooperation. Their alumni network is deeply embedded in the intelligence community. If Cape received a National Security Letter or FISA warrant demanding a backdoor:

\- Would they even be \*allowed\* to tell users?
\- Could they refuse without destroying the company?
\- Do they have any technical architecture that \*prevents\* compliance even if ordered?

The search results don't answer any of this.

\### 3. Funding Sources with Intelligence Ties

\- In-Q-Tel connections — Palantir was funded by In-Q-Tel (CIA). The alumni network maintains those relationships.
\- Bain Capital Ventures — has historical ties to defense and intelligence portfolios
\- Andreessen Horowitz — has invested in multiple defense/security companies with government contracts

These investors aren't privacy activists. They're institutional players with government relationships.

\### 4. No Transparency on Government Requests

Cape claims they don't collect data that could be handed over. But:

\- Have they \*received\* any government requests?
\- What's their legal battle history?
\- Do they publish transparency reports like Signal or Apple?

The search results show zero mention of transparency reporting.

\### 5. $900M Valuation After 2 Months GA

They went live in January 2026. By March 2026 they're valued at $900 million.^3^ That kind of rapid valuation suggests investors expect massive returns—which means mass adoption. Mass adoption of a "privacy" phone is exactly what intelligence agencies would want to monitor or infiltrate.

\---

\## The Honeypot Question

I'm not saying Cape \*is\* a honeypot. But the ingredients are there:

| Factor | Concern Level |
|--------|---------------|
| Palantir alumni | High |
| Rapid VC funding from defense-tied investors | High |
| No transparency reports | Medium-High |
| No independent security audits cited | High |
| New company with no track record | High |
| High-value target for government infiltration | High |

\---

\## What Cape Should Do (If Legitimate)

If they're serious about privacy and want to dispel these concerns:

1\. Publish warrant canaries — legal notices that disappear if they receive a gag order
2\. Third-party security audits — from reputable firms, made public
3\. Transparency reports — like Signal publishes regularly
4\. Open-source components — allow independent verification of critical architecture
5\. Explain the Palantir connection — address why surveillance alumni are now privacy advocates

None of this appears in the search results.

\---

\## Your Instinct Is Warranted

### Mat.I — 2026-04-08T00:59:55+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/alligator-clips-for-grounding-electric-fields.32517/post-370429>

> [Mr.AJ said:](/goto/post?id=370420)
>
> Does anyone have a good brand and/or amazon link for a reliable pair of alligator clips + grounding rod to ground a laptop? Particularly ones that would fit between the ethernet/power cables securely?

Many cheap ways to ground.. some e.g. you can make your own usb grounding cords. When network is not grounded. I make a usb grounding cord and bond the sheild/gnd to an outlet plug via a cable. Obviously only terminate the ground at the outlet plug end.. or go straight to stake in ground.. or... get a 3 prong charger and check continuity from earth prong to 0v terminal.. what brand laptop do you have?

### Mat.I — 2026-04-08T02:37:04+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/alligator-clips-for-grounding-electric-fields.32517/post-370435>

> [Mat.I said:](/goto/post?id=370429)
>
> Many cheap ways to ground.. some e.g. you can make your own usb grounding cords. When network is not grounded. I make a usb grounding cord and bond the sheild/gnd to an outlet plug via a cable. Obviously only terminate the ground at the outlet plug end.. or go straight to stake in ground.. or... get a 3 prong charger and check continuity from earth prong to 0v terminal.. what brand laptop do you have?

Also, to do it properly and clean (if making own gnd cords) include a 1M Ohm resistor in series. This is evident when you check 3 prong PSU to 0V resistance.. It acts as a safety feature so your device does not become part of the fault current path (under fault conditions) etc.. I have tested both ways and there was no difference in EF strength based on my n=1.. So best practice is to "soft" bond via a 1M Ohm resistor to avoid any low impedance bonds that can create hazards under certain fault conditions...

### Mat.I — 2026-04-08T07:44:10+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/alligator-clips-for-grounding-electric-fields.32517/post-370464>

> [jaedyn said:](/goto/post?id=370462)
>
> What are you using to plug into the earth pin of a GPO? Looking to do this myself, thanks for mentioning the resistor.

(ignore AS3000 for a moment)... Standard 3 pin plug end.. Just connect E only. For thickness to fit in gland end use circ or equivalent (only terminate earth only).. If being fancy you can knock the A + N pins out of socket and glue in plastic ones from child safe GPO protectors (as dummy pins).. But IMO they are not strong and could cause more of a hazard if broken and gets in the hands of a "lay" person.. You will find for most if not all devices you can somehow adapt a 3 prong factory PSU that is earthed. for e.g. majority of lenovo's have this standard.. What device have you got?

### Mat.I — 2026-04-09T00:51:27+0300

If no sheilded cable no need to worry unless you are strategically draining router to switch due to the 2 prong psu..

She is 65 and has always lived near Barcelona (41°N), 10km far away from the airport.
About 25 years ago they removed 3/4 of her thyroid gland due to a nodule. Since then taking Levotiroxina 50mg. All this time T3 and T4 have been in the accepted ranges of centralized medicine.
She got the AstraZeneca jabs.
A few years ago she got detected very slight cataracts.

A couple of years ago she started to use hearing aids, which may be used directly as headphones, so they are always blasting bluetooth. Also she used the Bluetooth a lot.
Some months ago she got checked because did not see well. Cataracts have advanced very quickly. In one eye she sees only 60%, in the other 80%.

She wears glasses with metal frame.

After reading the blog on cataracts some weeks ago, and seeing a Simulation of metal frame glasses that [@Rusty](https://forum.jackkruse.com/members/26197/) put on twitter with metal frame glasses, it is no wonder cataracts advanced so quickly.

She also tells me she has dry skin and insomnia.

For the last 6 months she installed red lights almost everywhere and wears blue blockers at night.

She has a beach appartment a bit further away from Barcelona so I told her to:
\- Do not use the hearing aids.
\- Move to the beach appartment (10-15km away from airport)
\- See the sunrise and stay at the beach grounded as long as possible.
\- Get new glasses without any UV/blue filter and with plastic frame.
\- Eat as much seafood as possible.
\- Try not to use much technology.

She also has a red lamp I gave her with 630, 670, 727, 810 and 850nm. Should she use it? If so, what protocol to use?**

Here some more questions that come to mind:

As long as I understand this is a redox problem partly or fully caused by electromagnetism. Reduced CCO productivity --> reduced water --> reduced heat sink (poor UPEs) --> brain does not want that --> hello cataracts.
What about using cold masks or "eye cold plunges" to cool the eyes now that she lacks metabollic water? Is it useless because is only for a short period of time? Or is it worth a try? If so, any idea on how often and how long to do it?

I guess guetting in the sea with the eyes under water would be great. But if she does not do that, is it worth it to lie down at the beach with eyes directly on the sand to ground near the eye, say, 30min daily?

I find it interesting that even with the redox problem, during the last year she was actually the most tanned in a while. It seems counterintuitive to me.

Any comment is appreciated!

# Thread: KYC + Biometric designed to make you more hackable
**Thread URL:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/kyc-biometric-designed-to-make-you-more-hackable.32594/unread>
**Subforum:** The Cave
**Posts:** 1
══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
### DLO — 2026-04-20T22:52:22+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/kyc-biometric-designed-to-make-you-more-hackable.32594/post-371605>

**Regulators spent the last few years demanding that banks, crypto exchanges, and fintech apps collect face scans, ID photos, and biometric templates from every customer. They sold this as a defense against financial crime. What it actually built was a global inventory of the most sensitive identifiers a person has, stored across thousands of corporate databases, waiting to be breached.**

Now the stolen contents of those databases power a thriving economy that lets money launderers walk through the front door of major banks wearing someone else’s face. The push toward biometric access and digital ID verification did not stop the fraud. It supplied the raw material for it.

A video reviewed by [MIT Technology Review](https://www.technologyreview.com/2026/04/15/1135898/cyberscammers-bypassing-bank-telegram/) shows the consequence in miniature. Somewhere inside a Cambodian scam compound, a worker opens a popular Vietnamese banking app, taps through the login flow, and reaches the liveness check. He holds up a static photo of a woman who looks nothing like the 30-something Asian man whose account he’s accessing. The app asks him to adjust the face in the frame. Ninety seconds later, he’s in.

That demonstration arrived from Hieu Minh Ngo, a former hacker turned cybersecurity advisor to the Vietnamese government who now investigates money laundering for an anti-scam nonprofit. The exploit he shared uses a virtual camera, a tool that replaces a phone’s live video feed with whatever the operator wants to show, whether a stolen photo, a deepfake, or a cardboard cutout of a stranger. Banks designed liveness checks to confirm a real person is sitting behind the screen. Virtual cameras make that confirmation meaningless.

The facial templates feeding those cameras had to come from somewhere. They came from the KYC (Know Your Customer) files that regulators required banks and exchanges to build. Face scans, passport photos, and liveness videos, once submitted to open an account, do not disappear. They accumulate in corporate archives governed by retention policies most users never read, and they leak through breaches, insider theft, and vendor compromises into the same Telegram marketplaces that sell the bypass kits.

Your face is your face. Your passport photo is your passport photo. Once those templates circulate online, they circulate forever, feeding every future fraud attempt against every future KYC system you encounter.

MIT Technology Review spent two months earlier this year cataloging that marketplace. The result was 22 public Telegram channels and groups operating in Chinese, Vietnamese, and English, hawking bypass kits and stolen biometric data to anyone willing to pay.

Some had thousands of subscribers. The bio of the program used by the Cambodian launderer read, “Specializing in bank services—handling dirty money,” finished with a thumbs-up emoji. “Secure. Professional. High quality.” The channels advertised services with bullet points like “All kinds of KYC verification services” and “It’s all smooth and seamless,” paired with videos purporting to show real bypasses.

Governments and financial institutions describe the underlying data hoarding as the price of stopping financial crime. The actual ledger looks different. Compliance requirements produced centralized collections of biometric data that cannot be changed after a leak. Passwords can be rotated. Credit cards can be reissued. Faces cannot. Every mandate that pushes more institutions to collect more biometric templates from more users expands the pool of permanently compromised identity data without giving anyone a way to claw it back.


══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

# Thread: The Soviet Sanatorium: 70 Years of Quantum Biology Hidden in Plain Sight
**Thread URL:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/the-soviet-sanatorium-70-years-of-quantum-biology-hidden-in-plain-sight.32608/unread>
**Subforum:** Feedback/Suggestions
**Posts:** 2
══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
### Iceland — 2026-04-22T02:18:07+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/the-soviet-sanatorium-70-years-of-quantum-biology-hidden-in-plain-sight.32608/post-371767>

While the West spent the last century perfecting the "**pill for an ill**" model, the Soviet Union—largely due to a lack of pharmaceutical infrastructure and a deep reverence for physics—focused on the **Sanatorium System**. These weren't luxury spas; they were **state-mandated medical facilities** designed to optimize the human semiconductor using Light, Water, and Magnetism.

For decades, the Soviets used environmental inputs to recharge the cellular battery. They mastered the physics of the environment because they couldn't afford the chemistry of the laboratory.

### 1\. Pelotherapy (The Original Full-Body Grounding)​

The Soviets engineered grounding into the very architecture of their sanatoriums. They used **Sapropel** (ancient, electrolyte-dense lake mud) as a conductive interface. By piping this mud directly from the earth through stone or metal systems and coating the patient in it, they created a massive, frictionless flow of electrons from the Earth’s crust into the human body. This was a 3D, heated, mineral-rich "liquid wire" that neutralized positive charge across 100% of the skin’s surface.

### 2\. Intravenous Laser Blood Irradiation (ILBI)​

Realizing the skin can act as a barrier to specific light frequencies, Soviet scientists invented **ILBI**. They developed fiber-optic needles to "inject" Red or UV light directly into the vein. As the blood circulated, it was "bathed" in photons, charging the mitochondria of every red and white blood cell. This turned the entire circulatory system into a light-harvesting antenna.

### 3\. Magnetotherapy and Zeta Potential​

Soviet doctors were obsessed with **Zeta Potential**—the electrical charge that keeps red blood cells from clumping. They used massive **PEMF (Pulsed Electromagnetic Field)** coils to "order" the water in the body and restore the magnetic field of damaged tissues, allowing for improved blood flow without chemical blood thinners.

### 4\. Intermittent Hypoxic-Hyperoxic Training (IHHT)​

The **"Revalit" Method** was a staple of Soviet sports and recovery medicine. By forcing patients to breathe low-oxygen air followed by bursts of high-oxygen air, they created a selective pressure that culled old, leaky mitochondria and triggered the birth of new, high-functioning ones.

### 5\. Speleotherapy (Radon and Salt Caves)​

Soviets utilized deep underground caves for **Radiation Hormesis**. They believed that controlled, trace exposure to ionizing radon gas triggered a massive endogenous repair response and DNA stabilization, forcing the body to upgrade its own antioxidant defense systems.

### 6\. The "Sharko" Shower (Hydro-Aero-Ionization)​

A technique involving high-pressure, high-contrast water hoses. It combined **Cold Thermogenesis** with the **Lenard Effect** (the creation of negative air ions from splashing water). The mechanical pressure and the temperature gradient forced an immediate "electron dump" into the peripheral nervous system.

### 7\. Quartz Lamp Clinics (Fractionated UV)​

In dark, northern latitudes, the Soviets didn't rely on Vitamin D pills. They built **"Quartz" clinics** where children and workers received mandatory, timed doses of UV light. They understood that humans are "light eaters" and that maintaining the photo-period was non-negotiable for circadian health.

### Why the US Needs a Decentralized Biophysics Revolution​

The modern US medical system is centralized around a biochemical model that is failing to address mitochondrial collapse and non-native EMF stress. If we want to solve the chronic disease crisis, we must move toward **Decentralized Medicine focused on Biophysics**.

The Soviets proved that you don't need a massive pharmaceutical supply chain to heal people; you need a deep understanding of how the human body interacts with the Earth's fields. The future of medicine isn't a new molecule—it's the restoration of our connection to physics.

### AlbertW — 2026-05-01T16:25:12+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/accessories-for-keeping-bluelight-blockers-from-falling-off-face.32625/post-372729>

There are some pads you can buy to attach to the nose bridge area to narrow the distance. That helps for my daughter.

# Thread: Kon-tiki - inspiration for a decentralized savage
**Thread URL:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/kon-tiki-inspiration-for-a-decentralized-savage.32638/unread>
**Subforum:** The Cave
**Posts:** 1
══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
### stuart31 — 2026-04-26T23:12:34+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/kon-tiki-inspiration-for-a-decentralized-savage.32638/post-372166>

I guess many people would have learned about this in grade school, but I just watched the documentary and am awestruck so thought to share with those not familiar. In 1947 these Norwegians used a simple raft made from balsa wood and rope to sail 5000 miles across the ocean from Peru to the French polynesian islands, apparently just to see if it was possible.

They describe how these consistent, steady winds, produced partially by the rotation of earth on its axis, could have assisted in humans populating these islands. This was in opposition to the accepted idea that they were populated by ships from Asia against the prevailing winds.

Along this 5000 mile voyage over 100+ days they were met by an ocean teeming with life which provided abundant seafood to eat. Flying fish would land helpless on the deck of their raft every morning providing them with breakfast. They could simply put a hook and line into the water and catch fish like nothing. Sharks were frequently encountered which they would bring aboard and kill them as protection from being eaten alive. They were able to avoid depleting their water supplies by drinking the lymph from larger fish which naturally filter out salt. They even caught cuttlefish to use as ink wells for writing in their journals. Interestingly enough they also brought a parrot with them on their voyage..

If nothing else, it's inspirational how these men were able to complete this fantastic feat without modern resources and technology but by harnessing nature's power. Once they set sail, they were unable to turn around even if they wanted to. They fully had their skin in the game. Once they were all in, it's almost as if nature provided for them along the way with provisions they never could have expected.

As I'm here constructing my own metaphorical life raft to get out of dodge, I can't help but wonder if this incredible expedition may carry some lessons about earth's magnetic field as well as being an inspirational story..


══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

# Thread: LifeLabs British Columbia sold your health records to blackrock
**Thread URL:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/lifelabs-british-columbia-sold-your-health-records-to-blackrock.32664/unread>
**Subforum:** The Cave
**Posts:** 1
══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
### DLO — 2026-04-30T06:27:07+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/lifelabs-british-columbia-sold-your-health-records-to-blackrock.32664/post-372615>

he Wall Street Takeover of BC Health Data: Your Blood Work Now Answers to Shareholders
ALEX HOSNER
APR 29, 2026
If you live in British Columbia, your provincial lab system is no longer a healthcare utility. It is a publicly traded asset, effectively owned by Wall Street mega-funds like Vanguard, BlackRock, and State Street.
This is not a political conspiracy; it is a structural and financial reality. In August 2024, the BC government rubber-stamped the sale of LifeLabs—the corporate entity responsible for processing 42 million lab tests annually for the province—for $1.35 billion CAD.
\--------
The Pension-to-Wall-Street Pipeline
Before 2024, LifeLabs was owned by OMERS—the Ontario Municipal Employees Retirement System. Ironically enough, when I started working on a drilling rig when I was 18, we spent 5 years drilling oil and gas wells for OMERS Energy.
OMERS is a massive Canadian pension fund. Their entire business model is built on acquiring and holding physical, long-term assets—whether those are natural gas wells or provincial medical labs—to guarantee stable, decades-long returns for Canadian municipal workers. Under OMERS, LifeLabs was operated as a utility. It was patient capital.
But in August 2024, that model was permanently dismantled. When OMERS sold LifeLabs to Quest Diagnostics for $1.35 billion CAD, we didn’t just trade one corporate logo for another. We traded patient Canadian capital for Wall Street extraction.
Quest Diagnostics isn’t interested in operating a stable, long-term utility. They are a publicly traded entity driven by institutional investors who demand aggressive, perpetual quarterly growth. The moment the ink dried on that sale, the BC lab system ceased to be a healthcare service and became a dividend engine.
To the average patient getting blood drawn, the logo on the door simply changed. But behind the scenes, the fundamental math of British Columbia’s healthcare system was violently rewritten. We traded Canadian pension fund ownership—which prioritizes slow, stable, long-term returns—for Wall Street institutional ownership, a beast that demands relentless, perpetual, and aggressive quarterly dividend growth.
Quest Diagnostics is not just a medical company; it is a $22 billion ticker symbol (DGX) on the New York Stock Exchange. When the fiduciary obligation to maximize shareholder returns sits directly between your doctor’s requisition and your test result, the degradation of patient care is not a mistake. It is a mathematical requirement.
\---------------------
Who Actually Owns Your Lab Tests? The Ownership Structure of DGX.
To understand how healthcare decisions are made under this model, you have to look at the cap table. Quest Diagnostics is a massive, publicly traded entity, and over 90% of its shares are held by institutional investors.
There is no “founder” steering the ship with a moral compass. There is no benevolent board of doctors protecting patient care. The company is owned, controlled, and dictated by the largest asset management funds on the planet.
As of early 2026, the top institutional shareholders of Quest Diagnostics (DGX) are:
The Vanguard Group: ~13.0%
BlackRock: ~8.5%
T. Rowe Price: ~5.7%
State Street Global Advisors: ~4.8%
JPMorgan Chase & Co: ~3.7%
If you combine Vanguard, BlackRock, and State Street, the “Big Three” index funds effectively control over a quarter of the entire voting power of the corporation.
Why does this matter? Because Vanguard and BlackRock do not manage healthcare; they manage wealth. Their fiduciary duty is to their fund investors, not to British Columbia’s patients. They vote on board members, executive compensation, and corporate strategy using a single, unified metric: maximizing shareholder return.
When the CEO of Quest Diagnostics looks at his quarterly dashboard, he isn’t answering to the BC Minister of Health. He is answering to Vanguard and BlackRock. And if swapping a comprehensive medical test for a cheaper, automated one increases the dividend yield, Vanguard will vote to keep the executive who made that swap and fire the one who didn’t.
\--------------------------------------------
The Math of the “Efficient Breach”
To understand what Wall Street ownership means for your health, you have to understand a concept in corporate law known as the “efficient breach”.
The efficient breach dictates that if substituting a cheaper, flawed process saves a corporation more money than it ultimately loses paying out settlements for the harm caused, doing so is not just an option—it is a calculated, legally defensible business decision. This is the exact math Ford Motor Company ran in their infamous internal memo when they calculated it was cheaper to let a certain number of people burn to death in Pinto fires than to spend the money fixing the gas tank design.
And it is the exact logic woven into the DNA of the company now running BC’s labs.
Quest Diagnostics has run this math before. In 2009, the US Department of Justice forced a Quest subsidiary (Nichols Institute Diagnostics) to pay a staggering $302 million settlement. The charge? They had knowingly manufactured, marketed, and sold faulty parathyroid hormone (PTH) test kits for six straight years. Doctors were using these inaccurate tests to make critical surgical and treatment decisions for patients with bone and kidney disease.
To a patient, six years of faulty tests is a medical catastrophe. To a massive publicly traded corporation, a $302 million fine for six years of elevated profit margins is simply a line item. It is the cost of doing business.
That same company now owns your blood work. And the shift toward “efficient” diagnostics in British Columbia has already begun.
\--------------------------------
The 6,149 Missing Diagnoses
The most glaring example of this efficiency mandate wasn’t about advancing medicine; it was about slashing labour costs at the expense of accuracy.
In late 2022, the BC Guidelines and Protocols Advisory Committee (GPAC) downgraded provincial stool testing. They mandated a shift from comprehensive, manual microscopy (the traditional Ova & Parasite test) to a cheaper, automated, multiplex PCR test called the Infectious Diarrhea Panel (IDP).
The financial logic is simple: Manual microscopy requires expensive human labour—technicians sitting at microscopes analyzing slides. Automated PCR tests do not. You feed the sample into a machine, and it spits out a result. It is high-volume, low-friction, and highly profitable.
But there is a medical cost. A peer-reviewed study published in the BC Medical Journal in March 2024 audited over 52,000 provincial stool specimens. They found 6,149 positive cases of parasites using the old manual method.
Because the new, automated IDP test only screens for a narrow list of specific, common pathogens, it completely misses the vast majority of those 6,000+ infections—specifically common but debilitating parasites like Blastocystis hominis and Dientamoeba fragilis.
Thousands of patients walking around with chronic gastrointestinal issues are now told their lab results are “negative,” simply because their specific pathogen didn’t make the “efficient” corporate list. A known diagnostic blind spot was codified into provincial protocol to save on human labour.
\----------------------------
Inventory, Not Patients: The Monetization of Biomarkers
The extraction of value under the Wall Street model doesn’t stop at the lab desk. It extends to the backend, where your biological data is transformed into a marketable asset.
Your blood sugar trends, cancer markers, hormone levels, and disease history are now held by a US corporation. Quest Diagnostics maintains that Canadian data stays on Canadian servers, but this is a legal sleight of hand. Because Quest is an American corporation, they are subject to the US CLOUD Act. This federal law allows American law enforcement and intelligence agencies to legally compel US-based companies to hand over data, regardless of where those servers are physically located in the world. British Columbia’s privacy laws cannot shield you from a US federal warrant issued to a Delaware corporation.
But the government isn’t the only one interested in your data. Quest openly markets a product called Commercial Alerts.
This product uses patient lab profiles to help pharmaceutical companies target doctors. According to their own marketing materials, a specific test order or biomarker result is the “first real-time indication of a potential candidate for a targeted therapy.” Quest uses this data to trigger alerts to pharmaceutical reps, allowing them to aggressively push specific drugs to your doctor at the exact moment your lab results come in.
Simultaneously, Quest is building an AI platform designed to monetize massive patient datasets in a global health-AI market projected to hit $1.03 trillion by 2030.35
Under this model, your lab results are not just medical records. They are inventory.
And the infrastructure holding that inventory is notoriously porous. In 2019, LifeLabs suffered a catastrophic data breach affecting 4.7 million BC residents—nearly the entire population of the province. They paid a ransom to hackers to retrieve the data. They spent four years fighting in court trying to bury the privacy commissioner’s investigation. Furthermore, they were found to have collected more personal information than the law allowed and failed to implement basic security safeguards.
The BC government’s response? They renewed the LifeLabs contract, and then approved the $1.35 billion sale to Wall Street.
\------------------------
The Anatomy of a Handover: Regulatory Capture
The BC government didn’t just stumble blindly into this American acquisition. The timeline proves they were lobbied, and they actively prepared the ground for it.
May 2, 2022: LifeLabs hosts an “Informational Reception” at the BC Legislature in Victoria. Public lobbying records show Health Minister Adrian Dix in attendance, alongside a massive list of MLAs and senior health bureaucrats.
July 2022: The BC government begins quietly outsourcing thousands of cervical cancer screenings (pap smears) directly to Quest Diagnostics in the United States This “pilot program” acted as the foot in the door, establishing the American corporation as a trusted, cross-border vendor for provincial health data.
October 2022: The provincial government downgrades provincial testing, implementing the automated IDP test and sacrificing thousands of accurate parasite diagnoses for operational efficiency, perfectly priming the system for an automated buyout.
August 2024: Quest Diagnostics officially buys LifeLabs, inheriting a lab system optimized for high-volume, low-labour profit extraction.
\---------------------------------
The $970 Million Dividend Machine
Quest expects its Canadian operations to generate $970 million CAD per year —revenue generated almost entirely from government contracts paid by your taxes.
Where does that money go? The financial pivot following the acquisition was immediate and aggressive. In early 2026, Quest authorized a $1.0 billion increase in stock buybacks and raised their shareholder dividend by 7.5%. Their CEO explicitly told investors the Canadian acquisition would be profitable in its very first year.
Your health tax dollars are being stripped from the BC medical system and converted directly into quarterly dividends for Vanguard, BlackRock, and State Street.
Your provincial government claims they are helpless. They state they are locked into this service contract until 2031 and cannot cancel it without triggering break clauses that would cost taxpayers “hundreds of millions of dollars.”
They built the trap, handed the keys to a Delaware corporation, and now tell the public they are stuck in it.
A recent poll found that 74% of BC residents oppose American ownership of their health services, and 77% want the government to intervene. The government knows this. They are counting on the public not connecting the timeline, the lobbying, the financial reports, and the missing diagnoses.
Healthcare in British Columbia has been financialized. Your health was never the priority. It was always the product.


══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

# Thread: feeling better already
**Thread URL:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/feeling-better-already.32707/unread>
**Subforum:** Success Stories
**Posts:** 1
══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
### Millerstef — 2026-05-06T23:04:45+0300
**Source:** <https://forum.jackkruse.com/threads/feeling-better-already.32707/post-373242>

I am a lifelong searcher for methods that can heal me. Always had trouble sleeping and had a very large intramuscular lipoma removed from my hamstring at 30. After having my first child at 32 and never getting enough sleep, I developed brain fog, symptoms of low thyroid but numbers are in range, low vitamin D, low cholesterol, slightly elevated bilirubin, low end for lymphocytes and arrythmias (even passed out a few times through the years) however heart appears perfectly normal when wearing holter monitor or having ekg, or ultrasound. I have tried every "natural" protocol under the sun and at times it seemed like I was on the right track. My supplement closet is insane. I started implementing some of Jack's protocols April 25th. I started to drink DDW at 2 to 1 ratio, spend as much time as I can with my feet on the ground in my yard and as weather permits wearing a bathing suit. I'm not able to catch most sunrises as it's quite early in Portland, Oregon but I get out with my feet on the ground as soon as the kids have breakfast and lunches packed. I have been outside for every sunset since the 25th. I have significantly cut down on my phone and screen time and am trying very hard to not use it for frivolous activities. I started chewing mastic gum, singing, humming, using my vibration plate daily, liberally applying dmso to my head in hopes of breaking up the lattice and jumping on the rebounder. I am eating some type of fish or crustacean 1 time a day and maybe even for a snack. Luckily I don't have a job that requires me to be on screens all day. My biggest improvement right now is I was having terrible brain fog and head pressure and my tinnitus that was triggered by a double ear infection about 5 years ago was increasing from very mild to more frequent. My head is feeling so much better, like a weight has been removed and my tinnitus is also getting better. I am excited to keep learning and implement all that I can on a daily basis. I'd love any feedback or tips people might like sharing aside from moving especially if you have delt with any of this and what works best for you.
